<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immune_system">Immune system</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">Immune system</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plant_disease_resistance" title="Plant disease resistance">Plant disease resistance</a></div>
<p>By means of cells that behave like <a href="/wiki/Nerve" title="Nerve">nerves</a>, plants receive and distribute within their systems information about incident light intensity and quality. Incident light that stimulates a chemical reaction in one leaf, will cause a chain reaction of signals to the entire plant via a type of cell termed a <i><a href="/wiki/Vascular_bundle" title="Vascular bundle">bundle sheath cell</a></i>. Researchers, from the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_University_of_Life_Sciences" title="Warsaw University of Life Sciences">Warsaw University of Life Sciences</a> in <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, found that plants have a specific memory for varying light conditions, which prepares their immune systems against seasonal pathogens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Plants use pattern-recognition receptors to recognize conserved microbial signatures. This recognition triggers an immune response. The first plant receptors of conserved microbial signatures were identified in <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> (XA21, 1995)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> and in <i><a href="/wiki/Arabidopsis_thaliana" title="Arabidopsis thaliana">Arabidopsis thaliana</a></i> (FLS2, 2000).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Plants also carry immune receptors that recognize highly variable pathogen effectors. These include the NBS-LRR class of proteins.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_distribution">Internal distribution</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-One_source plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-one_source" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="Question book-new.svg" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>relies largely or entirely upon a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">single source</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Plant##" title="Talk:Plant">talk page</a>. Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Plant&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by introducing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> to additional sources.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vascular_tissue" title="Vascular tissue">Vascular tissue</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Vascular_plant" title="Vascular plant">Vascular plants</a> differ from other plants in that nutrients are transported between their different parts through specialized structures, called <a href="/wiki/Xylem" title="Xylem">xylem</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phloem" title="Phloem">phloem</a>. They also have <a href="/wiki/Root" title="Root">roots</a> for taking up water and minerals. The xylem moves water and minerals from the root to the rest of the plant, and the phloem provides the roots with sugars and other nutrient produced by the leaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Genomics">Genomics</span></h2>
<p>Plants have some of the largest <a href="/wiki/Genome" title="Genome">genomes</a> among all organisms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The largest plant genome (in terms of gene number) is that of <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a> (<i>Triticum asestivum</i>), predicted to encode ≈94,000 genes<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> and thus almost 5 times as many as the <a href="/wiki/Human_genome" title="Human genome">human genome</a>. The first plant genome sequenced was that of <i><a href="/wiki/Arabidopsis_thaliana" title="Arabidopsis thaliana">Arabidopsis thaliana</a></i> which encodes about 25,500 genes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> In terms of sheer DNA sequence, the smallest published genome is that of the carnivorous <a href="/wiki/Utricularia_gibba" title="Utricularia gibba">bladderwort</a> (<i>Utricularia gibba)</i> at 82 Mb (although it still encodes 28,500 genes)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> while the largest, from the <a href="/wiki/Picea_abies" title="Picea abies">Norway Spruce</a> (<i>Picea abies</i>), extends over 19,600 Mb (encoding about 28,300 genes).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Plant_ecology" title="Plant ecology">Plant ecology</a></div>
<p>The photosynthesis conducted by land plants and algae is the ultimate source of energy and organic material in nearly all ecosystems. Photosynthesis, at first by cyanobacteria and later by photosynthetic eukaryotes, radically changed the composition of the early Earth's anoxic atmosphere, which as a result is now 21% <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a>. Animals and most other organisms are <a href="/wiki/Aerobic_organism" title="Aerobic organism">aerobic</a>, relying on oxygen; those that do not are confined to relatively rare <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anaerobic_environment" title="Anaerobic environment">anaerobic environments</a>. Plants are the <a href="/wiki/Autotroph" title="Autotroph">primary producers</a> in most terrestrial ecosystems and form the basis of the <a href="/wiki/Food_web" title="Food web">food web</a> in those ecosystems. Many animals rely on plants for shelter as well as oxygen and food.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Plants form about 80% of the world <a href="/wiki/Biomass_(ecology)" title="Biomass (ecology)">biomass</a> at about 450 gigatonnes (4.4<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>11</sup> long tons; 5.0<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>11</sup> short tons) of carbon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bar-On_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bar-On-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>Land plants are key components of the <a href="/wiki/Water_cycle" title="Water cycle">water cycle</a> and several other <a href="/wiki/Biogeochemical_cycle" title="Biogeochemical cycle">biogeochemical cycles</a>. Some plants have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coevolve" title="Coevolve">coevolved</a> with <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_fixation" title="Nitrogen fixation">nitrogen fixing</a> bacteria, making plants an important part of the <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_cycle" title="Nitrogen cycle">nitrogen cycle</a>. Plant roots play an essential role in <a href="/wiki/Soil" title="Soil">soil</a> development and the prevention of <a href="/wiki/Soil_erosion" title="Soil erosion">soil erosion</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution">Distribution</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Plant&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Plants are distributed almost worldwide. While they inhabit a multitude of <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">biomes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a>, few can be found beyond the <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundras</a> at the northernmost regions of <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">continental shelves</a>. At the southern extremes, plants of the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_flora" title="Antarctic flora">Antarctic flora</a> have adapted tenaciously to the prevailing conditions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Plants are often the dominant physical and structural component of habitats where they occur. Many of the Earth's <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">biomes</a> are named for the type of vegetation because plants are the dominant organisms in those biomes, such as <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grasslands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">taiga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rainforest</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecological_relationships">Ecological relationships</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Venus_Flytrap_showing_trigger_hairs.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1670" data-file-width="1527" decoding="async" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Venus_Flytrap_showing_trigger_hairs.jpg/220px-Venus_Flytrap_showing_trigger_hairs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Venus_Flytrap_showing_trigger_hairs.jpg/330px-Venus_Flytrap_showing_trigger_hairs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Venus_Flytrap_showing_trigger_hairs.jpg/440px-Venus_Flytrap_showing_trigger_hairs.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Venus_Flytrap_showing_trigger_hairs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Venus_flytrap" title="Venus flytrap">Venus flytrap</a>, a species of <a href="/wiki/Carnivorous_plant" title="Carnivorous plant">carnivorous plant</a>.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Plant&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2018</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Numerous animals have coevolved with plants. Many animals <a href="/wiki/Pollination" title="Pollination">pollinate</a> <a href="/wiki/Flower" title="Flower">flowers</a> in exchange for food in the form of pollen or <a href="/wiki/Nectar" title="Nectar">nectar</a>. Many animals <a href="/wiki/Biological_dispersal" title="Biological dispersal">disperse seeds</a>, often by eating <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruit</a> and passing the seeds in their <a href="/wiki/Feces" title="Feces">feces</a>. <a href="/wiki/Myrmecophyte" title="Myrmecophyte">Myrmecophytes</a> are plants that have coevolved with <a href="/wiki/Ant" title="Ant">ants</a>. The plant provides a home, and sometimes food, for the ants. In exchange, the ants defend the plant from <a href="/wiki/Herbivore" title="Herbivore">herbivores</a> and sometimes competing plants. Ant wastes provide organic <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizer</a>.
</p><p>The majority of plant species have various kinds of fungi associated with their root systems in a kind of <a href="/wiki/Mutualism_(biology)" title="Mutualism (biology)">mutualistic</a> <a href="/wiki/Symbiosis" title="Symbiosis">symbiosis</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Mycorrhiza" title="Mycorrhiza">mycorrhiza</a>. The fungi help the plants gain water and mineral nutrients from the soil, while the plant gives the fungi carbohydrates manufactured in photosynthesis. Some plants serve as homes for <a href="/wiki/Endophyte" title="Endophyte">endophytic</a> fungi that protect the plant from herbivores by producing toxins. The fungal endophyte, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neotyphodium_coenophialum" title="Neotyphodium coenophialum">Neotyphodium coenophialum</a></i>, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tall_fescue" title="Tall fescue">tall fescue</a> (<i>Festuca arundinacea</i>) does tremendous economic damage to the cattle industry in the U.S. Many legume plants have nitrogen fixing bacteria in the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Rhizobium" title="Rhizobium">Rhizobium</a></i>, found in nodules of their roots, that fix nitrogen from the air for the plant to use. In exchange, the plants supply sugars to the bacteria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>
</p><p>Various forms of parasitism are also fairly common among plants, from the semi-parasitic <a href="/wiki/Mistletoe" title="Mistletoe">mistletoe</a> that merely takes some nutrients from its host, but still has photosynthetic leaves, to the fully parasitic <a href="/wiki/Orobanche" title="Orobanche">broomrape</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lathraea" title="Lathraea">toothwort</a> that acquire all their nutrients through connections to the roots of other plants, and so have no <a href="/wiki/Chlorophyll" title="Chlorophyll">chlorophyll</a>. Some plants, known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myco-heterotroph" title="Myco-heterotroph">myco-heterotrophs</a>, parasitize mycorrhizal fungi, and hence act as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epiparasite" title="Epiparasite">epiparasites</a> on other plants.
</p><p>Many plants are <a href="/wiki/Epiphyte" title="Epiphyte">epiphytes</a>, meaning they grow on other plants, usually trees, without parasitizing them. Epiphytes may indirectly harm their host plant by intercepting mineral nutrients and light that the host would otherwise receive. The weight of large numbers of epiphytes may break tree limbs. <a href="/wiki/Hemiepiphyte" title="Hemiepiphyte">Hemiepiphytes</a> like the <a href="/wiki/Strangler_fig" title="Strangler fig">strangler fig</a> begin as epiphytes but eventually set their own roots and overpower and kill their host. Many <a href="/wiki/Orchid" title="Orchid">orchids</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bromeliad" title="Bromeliad">bromeliads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fern" title="Fern">ferns</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moss" title="Moss">mosses</a> often grow as epiphytes. Bromeliad epiphytes accumulate water in leaf axils to form <a href="/wiki/Phytotelma" title="Phytotelma">phytotelmata</a> that may contain complex aquatic food webs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>
</p><p>Approximately 630 plants are <a href="/wiki/Carnivorous_plant" title="Carnivorous plant">carnivorous</a>, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venus_Flytrap" title="Venus Flytrap">Venus Flytrap</a> (<i>Dionaea muscipula</i>) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sundew" title="Sundew">sundew</a> (<i>Drosera</i> species). They trap small animals and digest them to obtain mineral nutrients, especially <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">nitrogen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phosphorus" title="Phosphorus">phosphorus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barthlott_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barthlott-94">[94]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span></h3>
<p>Competition occurs when members of the same species, or several different species, compete for shared resources in a given habitat. According to the competitive exclusion principle, when environmental resources are limited, species cannot occupy nor be supported by identical niches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-95">[95]</a></sup> Eventually, one species will out-compete the other, which will push the disadvantaged species to extinction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-95">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>In regard to plants, competition tends to negatively affect their growth when competing for shared resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-96">[96]</a></sup> These shared resources commonly include space for growth, sunlight, water and nutrients. Light is an important resource because it is necessary for photosynthesis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-96">[96]</a></sup> Plants use their leaves to shade other plants from sunlight and grow quickly to maximize their own expose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_96-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-96">[96]</a></sup> Water is also important for photosynthesis, and plants have different root systems to maximize water uptake from soil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-97">[97]</a></sup> Some plants have deep roots that are able to locate water stored deep underground, and others have shallower roots that are capable of extending longer distances to collect recent rainwater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>Minerals are also important for plant growth and development, where deficiencies can occur if nutrient needs are not met.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Common nutrients competed for amongst plants include nitrogen and phosphorus. Space is also extremely important for a growing and developing plant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-99">[99]</a></sup> Having optimal space makes it more likely that leaves are exposed to sufficient amounts of sunlight and are not overcrowded in order for photosynthesis to occur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-99">[99]</a></sup> If an old tree dies, then competition arises amongst a number of trees to replace it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_96-3"><a href="#cite_note-:1-96">[96]</a></sup> Those that are less effective competitors are less likely to contribute to the next generation of offspring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_96-4"><a href="#cite_note-:1-96">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>Contrary to the belief that plants are always in competition, new research has found that in a harsh environment mature plants sheltering seedlings help the smaller plant survive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Importance">Importance</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plants_in_culture" title="Plants in culture">Plants in culture</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultivation">Cultivation<span class="anchor" id="Production"></span></span></h3>
<p>The study of plant uses by people is called economic botany or <a href="/wiki/Ethnobotany" title="Ethnobotany">ethnobotany</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Human cultivation of plants is part of <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, which is the basis of human civilization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plant_agriculture" title="Plant agriculture">Plant agriculture</a></i> is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Agronomy" title="Agronomy">agronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horticulture" title="Horticulture">horticulture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Harvest_Time_-_geograph.org.uk_-_747095.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Harvest_Time_-_geograph.org.uk_-_747095.jpg/220px-Harvest_Time_-_geograph.org.uk_-_747095.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Harvest_Time_-_geograph.org.uk_-_747095.jpg/330px-Harvest_Time_-_geograph.org.uk_-_747095.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Harvest_Time_-_geograph.org.uk_-_747095.jpg/440px-Harvest_Time_-_geograph.org.uk_-_747095.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Harvest_Time_-_geograph.org.uk_-_747095.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mechanical harvest of oats.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a></div>
<p>Humans depend on plants for <a href="/wiki/Food" title="Food">food</a>, either directly or as feed for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domestic_animal" title="Domestic animal">domestic animals</a>. <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a> deals with the production of food crops, and has <a href="/wiki/History_of_agriculture" title="History of agriculture">played a key role in the history of world civilizations</a>. Agriculture includes <a href="/wiki/Agronomy" title="Agronomy">agronomy</a> for arable crops, <a href="/wiki/Horticulture" title="Horticulture">horticulture</a> for vegetables and fruit, and <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a> for timber.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NatGeogAgriculture_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-NatGeogAgriculture-104">[104]</a></sup> About 7,000 species of plant have been used for food, though most of today's food is derived from only 30 species. The major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Staple_crop" title="Staple crop">staples</a> include <a href="/wiki/Cereal" title="Cereal">cereals</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, starchy roots and tubers such as <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potato</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Legume" title="Legume">legumes</a> such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peas" title="Peas">peas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">beans</a>. <a href="/wiki/Vegetable_oil" title="Vegetable oil">Vegetable oils</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Olive_oil" title="Olive oil">olive oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a> provide <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lipids" title="Lipids">lipids</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vegetable" title="Vegetable">vegetables</a> contribute <a href="/wiki/Vitamin" title="Vitamin">vitamins</a> and minerals to the diet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medicines">Medicines</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Medicinal_plants" title="Medicinal plants">Medicinal plants</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Melocactus_as_a_medicine.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Melocactus_as_a_medicine.jpg/220px-Melocactus_as_a_medicine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Melocactus_as_a_medicine.jpg/330px-Melocactus_as_a_medicine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Melocactus_as_a_medicine.jpg/440px-Melocactus_as_a_medicine.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Melocactus_as_a_medicine.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Melocactus" title="Melocactus">Melocactus</a> plants being used as medicine.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Medicinal_plants" title="Medicinal plants">Medicinal plants</a> are a primary source of <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">organic compounds</a>, both for their medicinal and physiological effects, and for the industrial <a href="/wiki/Organic_synthesis" title="Organic synthesis">synthesis</a> of a vast array of organic chemicals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Many hundreds of medicines are derived from plants, both traditional medicines used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herbalism" title="Herbalism">herbalism</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tapsell_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-tapsell-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lai_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-lai-108">[108]</a></sup> and chemical substances purified from plants or first identified in them, sometimes by <a href="/wiki/Ethnobotany" title="Ethnobotany">ethnobotanical</a> search, and then <a href="/wiki/Organic_synthesis" title="Organic synthesis">synthesised</a> for use in modern medicine. Modern medicines derived from plants include <a href="/wiki/Aspirin" title="Aspirin">aspirin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taxol" title="Taxol">taxol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morphine" title="Morphine">morphine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quinine" title="Quinine">quinine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reserpine" title="Reserpine">reserpine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colchicine" title="Colchicine">colchicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digitalis" title="Digitalis">digitalis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vincristine" title="Vincristine">vincristine</a>. <a href="/wiki/List_of_plants_used_in_herbalism" title="List of plants used in herbalism">Plants used in herbalism</a> include <a href="/wiki/Ginkgo_biloba" title="Ginkgo biloba">ginkgo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Echinacea" title="Echinacea">echinacea</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feverfew" title="Feverfew">feverfew</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_John%27s_wort" title="Saint John's wort">Saint John's wort</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Pharmacopoeia" title="Pharmacopoeia">pharmacopoeia</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dioscorides" title="Dioscorides">Dioscorides</a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/De_Materia_Medica" title="De Materia Medica">De Materia Medica</a></i>, describing some 600 medicinal plants, was written between 50 and 70 AD and remained in use in Europe and the Middle East until around 1600 AD; it was the precursor of all modern pharmacopoeias.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIH-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nonfood_products">Nonfood products</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Timber_DonnellyMills2005_SeanMcClean.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Timber_DonnellyMills2005_SeanMcClean.jpg/220px-Timber_DonnellyMills2005_SeanMcClean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Timber_DonnellyMills2005_SeanMcClean.jpg/330px-Timber_DonnellyMills2005_SeanMcClean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Timber_DonnellyMills2005_SeanMcClean.jpg/440px-Timber_DonnellyMills2005_SeanMcClean.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Timber_DonnellyMills2005_SeanMcClean.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timber" title="Timber">Timber</a> in storage for later processing at a <a href="/wiki/Sawmill" title="Sawmill">sawmill</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-food_crop" title="Non-food crop">Non-food crop</a></div>
<p>Plants grown as industrial crops are the source of a wide range of products used in manufacturing, sometimes so intensively as to risk harm to the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Nonfood products include <a href="/wiki/Essential_oil" title="Essential oil">essential oils</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natural_dye" title="Natural dye">natural dyes</a>, pigments, <a href="/wiki/Wax" title="Wax">waxes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Resin" title="Resin">resins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tannin" title="Tannin">tannins</a>, alkaloids, <a href="/wiki/Amber" title="Amber">amber</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cork_material" title="Cork material">cork</a>. Products derived from plants include soaps, shampoos, perfumes, cosmetics, paint, varnish, turpentine, rubber, <a href="/wiki/Latex" title="Latex">latex</a>, lubricants, linoleum, plastics, inks, and <a href="/wiki/Gum_(botany)" title="Gum (botany)">gums</a>. Renewable fuels from plants include <a href="/wiki/Firewood" title="Firewood">firewood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuels</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CruzDierig2014_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-CruzDierig2014-114">[114]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a> <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> are derived from the remains of aquatic organisms including <a href="/wiki/Phytoplankton" title="Phytoplankton">phytoplankton</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geological_time" title="Geological time">geological time</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>Structural resources and fibres from plants are used to construct dwellings and to manufacture clothing. <a href="/wiki/Wood" title="Wood">Wood</a> is used not only for buildings, boats, and furniture, but also for smaller items such as <a href="/wiki/Musical_instrument" title="Musical instrument">musical instruments</a> and sports equipment. Wood is <a href="/wiki/Pulp_(paper)" title="Pulp (paper)">pulped</a> to make paper and cardboard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Cloth is often made from <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flax" title="Flax">flax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ramie" title="Ramie">ramie</a> or synthetic fibres such as <a href="/wiki/Rayon" title="Rayon">rayon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acetate" title="Acetate">acetate</a> derived from plant <a href="/wiki/Cellulose" title="Cellulose">cellulose</a>. <a href="/wiki/Thread_(yarn)" title="Thread (yarn)">Thread</a> used to sew cloth likewise comes in large part from cotton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aesthetic_uses">Aesthetic uses</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rose_espalier_Niedernhall.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2616" data-file-width="3488" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rose_espalier_Niedernhall.JPG/220px-Rose_espalier_Niedernhall.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rose_espalier_Niedernhall.JPG/330px-Rose_espalier_Niedernhall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rose_espalier_Niedernhall.JPG/440px-Rose_espalier_Niedernhall.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rose_espalier_Niedernhall.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A rose <a href="/wiki/Espalier" title="Espalier">espalier</a> at Niedernhall in Germany.</div></div></div>
<p>Thousands of plant species are cultivated for aesthetic purposes as well as to provide shade, modify temperatures, reduce wind, abate noise, provide privacy, and prevent soil erosion. Plants are the basis of a multibillion-dollar per year tourism industry, which includes travel to <a href="/wiki/Garden_tourism" title="Garden tourism">historic gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national parks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">forests</a> with colorful autumn leaves, and festivals such as <a href="/wiki/Hanami" title="Hanami">Japan's</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/National_Cherry_Blossom_Festival" title="National Cherry Blossom Festival">America's cherry blossom festivals</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCBF_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-NCBF-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Luxor,_West_Bank,_Ramesseum,_column_top_decorations,_Egypt,_Oct_2004.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="853" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Luxor%2C_West_Bank%2C_Ramesseum%2C_column_top_decorations%2C_Egypt%2C_Oct_2004.jpg/220px-Luxor%2C_West_Bank%2C_Ramesseum%2C_column_top_decorations%2C_Egypt%2C_Oct_2004.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Luxor%2C_West_Bank%2C_Ramesseum%2C_column_top_decorations%2C_Egypt%2C_Oct_2004.jpg/330px-Luxor%2C_West_Bank%2C_Ramesseum%2C_column_top_decorations%2C_Egypt%2C_Oct_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Luxor%2C_West_Bank%2C_Ramesseum%2C_column_top_decorations%2C_Egypt%2C_Oct_2004.jpg/440px-Luxor%2C_West_Bank%2C_Ramesseum%2C_column_top_decorations%2C_Egypt%2C_Oct_2004.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Luxor,_West_Bank,_Ramesseum,_column_top_decorations,_Egypt,_Oct_2004.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Capitals of ancient Egyptian columns decorated to resemble <a href="/wiki/Cyperus_papyrus" title="Cyperus papyrus">papyrus</a> plants. (at Luxor, Egypt)</div></div></div>
<p>While some <a href="/wiki/Garden" title="Garden">gardens</a> are planted with food crops, many are planted for aesthetic, ornamental, or conservation purposes. <a href="/wiki/Arboretum" title="Arboretum">Arboretums</a> and <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical gardens</a> are public collections of living plants. In private outdoor gardens, lawn grasses, shade trees, ornamental trees, shrubs, vines, herbaceous perennials and bedding plants are used. Gardens may cultivate the plants in a naturalistic state, or may sculpture their growth, as with <a href="/wiki/Topiary" title="Topiary">topiary</a> or <a href="/wiki/Espalier" title="Espalier">espalier</a>. <a href="/wiki/Gardening" title="Gardening">Gardening</a> is the most popular leisure activity in the U.S., and working with plants or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horticulture_therapy" title="Horticulture therapy">horticulture therapy</a> is beneficial for rehabilitating people with disabilities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Plants may also be grown or kept indoors as <a href="/wiki/Houseplant" title="Houseplant">houseplants</a>, or in specialized buildings such as <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse" title="Greenhouse">greenhouses</a> that are designed for the care and cultivation of living plants. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venus_Flytrap" title="Venus Flytrap">Venus Flytrap</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sensitive_plant" title="Sensitive plant">sensitive plant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Resurrection_plant" title="Resurrection plant">resurrection plant</a> are examples of plants sold as novelties. There are also art forms specializing in the arrangement of cut or living plant, such as <a href="/wiki/Bonsai" title="Bonsai">bonsai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ikebana" title="Ikebana">ikebana</a>, and the arrangement of cut or dried flowers. <a href="/wiki/Ornamental_plant" title="Ornamental plant">Ornamental plants</a> have sometimes changed the course of history, as in <a href="/wiki/Tulip_mania" title="Tulip mania">tulipomania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lambert_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lambert-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p><p>Architectural designs resembling plants appear in the capitals of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Ancient Egyptian</a> columns, which were carved to resemble either the <a href="/wiki/Nymphaea_lotus" title="Nymphaea lotus">Egyptian white lotus</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Cyperus_papyrus" title="Cyperus papyrus">papyrus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Images of plants are often used in painting and photography, as well as on textiles, money, stamps, flags and coats of arms.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_and_cultural_uses">Scientific and cultural uses</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barbara_McClintock_(1902-1992)_shown_in_her_laboratory_in_1947.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1833" decoding="async" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Barbara_McClintock_%281902-1992%29_shown_in_her_laboratory_in_1947.jpg/220px-Barbara_McClintock_%281902-1992%29_shown_in_her_laboratory_in_1947.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Barbara_McClintock_%281902-1992%29_shown_in_her_laboratory_in_1947.jpg/330px-Barbara_McClintock_%281902-1992%29_shown_in_her_laboratory_in_1947.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Barbara_McClintock_%281902-1992%29_shown_in_her_laboratory_in_1947.jpg/440px-Barbara_McClintock_%281902-1992%29_shown_in_her_laboratory_in_1947.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Barbara_McClintock_(1902-1992)_shown_in_her_laboratory_in_1947.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Barbara McClintock (1902–1992) was a pioneering <a href="/wiki/Cytogenetics" title="Cytogenetics">cytogeneticist</a> who used <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a> (corn) to study the mechanism of inheritance of traits.</div></div></div>
<p>Basic biological research has often been done with plants. In <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetics</a>, the breeding of pea plants allowed <a href="/wiki/Gregor_Mendel" title="Gregor Mendel">Gregor Mendel</a> to derive the basic laws governing inheritance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> and examination of <a href="/wiki/Chromosome" title="Chromosome">chromosomes</a> in maize allowed <a href="/wiki/Barbara_McClintock" title="Barbara McClintock">Barbara McClintock</a> to demonstrate their connection to inherited traits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The plant <i><a href="/wiki/Arabidopsis_thaliana" title="Arabidopsis thaliana">Arabidopsis thaliana</a></i> is used in laboratories as a <a href="/wiki/Model_organism" title="Model organism">model organism</a> to understand how <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">genes</a> control the growth and development of plant structures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> predicts that space stations or space colonies will one day rely on plants for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Controlled_Ecological_Life_Support_System" title="Controlled Ecological Life Support System">life support</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ancient trees are revered and many are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_famous_trees" title="List of famous trees">famous</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tree_ring" title="Tree ring">Tree rings</a> themselves are an important method of dating in archeology, and serve as a record of past climates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>Plants figure prominently in <a href="/wiki/Trees_in_mythology" title="Trees in mythology">mythology</a>, religion and <a href="/wiki/List_of_fictional_plants" title="List of fictional plants">literature</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> They are used as <a href="/wiki/National_emblem" title="National emblem">national</a> and state emblems, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_trees" title="List of U.S. state trees">state trees</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_flower" title="State flower">state flowers</a>. Plants are often used as memorials, gifts and to mark special occasions such as births, deaths, weddings and holidays. The arrangement of flowers may be used to send hidden <a href="/wiki/Language_of_flowers" title="Language of flowers">messages</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Negative_effects">Negative effects</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Texas_invasive_Musk_Thistle_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2103" data-file-width="2152" decoding="async" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Texas_invasive_Musk_Thistle_1.jpg/220px-Texas_invasive_Musk_Thistle_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Texas_invasive_Musk_Thistle_1.jpg/330px-Texas_invasive_Musk_Thistle_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Texas_invasive_Musk_Thistle_1.jpg/440px-Texas_invasive_Musk_Thistle_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Texas_invasive_Musk_Thistle_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Carduus_nutans" title="Carduus nutans">Musk Thistle</a> are invasive species in <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">texas</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Weed" title="Weed">Weeds</a> are commercially or aesthetically undesirable plants growing in managed environments such as <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">farms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban areas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garden" title="Garden">gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lawn" title="Lawn">lawns</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Park" title="Park">parks</a>. People have spread plants beyond their native ranges and some of these introduced plants become <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasive</a>, damaging existing ecosystems by displacing native species, and sometimes becoming serious weeds of cultivation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Plants may cause harm to animals, including people. Plants that produce <a href="/wiki/Anemophily" title="Anemophily">windblown pollen</a> invoke allergic reactions in people who suffer from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hay_fever" title="Hay fever">hay fever</a>. A wide variety of plants are <a href="/wiki/List_of_poisonous_plants" title="List of poisonous plants">poisonous</a>. <a href="/wiki/Toxalbumin" title="Toxalbumin">Toxalbumins</a> are plant poisons fatal to most mammals and act as a serious deterrent to consumption. Several plants cause skin irritations when touched, such as <a href="/wiki/Poison_ivy" title="Poison ivy">poison ivy</a>. Certain plants contain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychotropic" title="Psychotropic">psychotropic</a> <a href="/wiki/Secondary_metabolite" title="Secondary metabolite">chemicals</a>, which are extracted and ingested or smoked, including <a href="/wiki/Nicotine" title="Nicotine">nicotine</a> from <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cannabinoids" title="Cannabinoids">cannabinoids</a> from <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_sativa" title="Cannabis sativa">Cannabis sativa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Erythroxylon_coca" title="Erythroxylon coca">Erythroxylon coca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Opium" title="Opium">opium</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opium_poppy" title="Opium poppy">opium poppy</a>. <a href="/wiki/Smoking" title="Smoking">Smoking</a> causes damage to health or even death, while some drugs may also be harmful or fatal to people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Both illegal and legal drugs derived from plants may have negative effects on the economy, affecting worker productivity and law enforcement costs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>
